"During WWI, 'shell shock' was a term used to describe what we now recognize as PTSD, affecting many soldiers mentally. The soldier in the image likely experienced severe psychological stress, a common issue due to the intense and prolonged combat conditions of WWI. The French military, like many others, initially misunderstood shell shock, often mistaking it for cowardice, leading to harsh disciplinary measures.
Treatment for shell shock during WWI included rest, removal from the front lines, and sometimes controversial methods like electrotherapy, with varying degrees of success. The recognition of shell shock as a legitimate medical condition marked a significant shift in how mental health was perceived in military contexts."
